## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in constitutive modeling. Stress typically increases with strain through hardening mechanisms and decreases with temperature through thermal softening.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (basic strain hardening without temperature)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal factor, c2 typically negative)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation-type hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (power hardening times linear thermal factor)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic plus plastic contribution)
- Polynomial hardening with thermal: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T) (polynomial strain dependence with linear temperature)
- Swift law with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine (Garofalo): sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (high-temperature creep/flow stress)
- Zener-Hollomon type: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T) + c3) (logarithmic stress from Zener-Hollomon parameter)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 * exp(c4 * T) (two-term constitutive model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type form: (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)), stress approaches a plateau at large strains
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → Separate strain and temperature terms as products: f(epsilon) * g(T)
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) where T is absolute temperature, indicating diffusion-controlled deformation
- Homologous temperature scaling → Linear thermal softening (1 - c*T) representing fraction of melting temperature
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear and power-law terms: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2, capturing both regimes
- Logarithmic stress dependence on strain rate/temperature → sinh or log forms appearing in high-temperature flow stress models
- Pre-strain or offset yield → Shifted power law (epsilon + c0)**c1 to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Competing hardening and recovery → Difference of terms: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(1-exp(-c3*epsilon)), representing work hardening vs dynamic recovery
